<div class="d-flex flex-row mb-3">
  <div class="flex-1" data-pjax="#repo-content-pjax-container">
    <h1 data-view-component="true" class="d-inline mr-3"><a href="/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/tag/v3.1.5" data-view-component="true" class="Link--primary">wxWidgets 3.1.5</a></h1>
    <a href="/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/latest" data-view-component="true" class="v-align-text-bottom d-none d-md-inline-block"><span data-view-component="true" class="Label Label--success Label--large">Latest</span></a>
      <div class="v-align-text-bottom ml-2 d-none d-md-inline">
          
      </div>
  </div>

  <div class="mt-3 d-md-none">
    <a href="/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/latest" data-view-component="true" class="v-align-text-bottom"><span data-view-component="true" class="Label Label--success Label--large">Latest</span></a>

            </div>

  </div>
        <div data-pjax="true" data-test-selector="body-content" data-view-component="true" class="markdown-body my-3"><p>Welcome to wxWidgets, a free and open source cross-platform C++ framework for writing advanced GUI applications using native controls.</p>
<p>wxWidgets 3.1.5 is the latest release in the 3.1 development branch. This release is a "development" one as it makes (very few) incompatible API changes compared to 3.0 and does not guarantee the ABI stability, unlike the 3.0.x series. It is not inherently more buggy or less stable than the "stable" releases and you're encouraged to use it, including in production. If you're already using 3.0, upgrading shouldn't require any special effort, so please try it out.</p>
<p>Please see <a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/v3.1.5/docs/readme.txt" rel="nofollow"><strong>README</strong></a> for more information about this release and the <a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/v3.1.5/docs/changes.txt" rel="nofollow">change log</a> for more details of the changes in it.</p>
<h2>Source Files and Documentation</h2>
<p>If you intend to build wxWidgets from sources (which is recommended), please do <strong>NOT</strong> download the files using the "Source code" links just above, which are automatically generated by GitHub and don't contain the submodules sources which are necessary for building wxWidgets.</p>
<p>Instead, download one of <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.5/wxWidgets-3.1.5.zip">wxWidgets-3.1.5.zip</a> or <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.5/wxWidgets-3.1.5.7z">wxWidgets-3.1.5.7z</a>, for much smaller size, for Microsoft Windows systems or <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.5/wxWidgets-3.1.5.tar.bz2">wxWidgets-3.1.5.tar.bz2</a> for Unix ones, including macOS. These archives have exactly the same contents, but use the line endings appropriate for the corresponding platform.</p>
<p>In addition, we provide archives containing the documentation in either HTML or Microsoft CHM formats. Notice that the documentation is also <a href="https://docs.wxwidgets.org/3.1.5" rel="nofollow">available online</a>.</p>
<p>Finally, Microsoft Windows users may download <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.5/wxMSW-3.1.5-Setup.exe">Setup.exe file</a> containing both sources and documentation, however please note that this file does <em>not</em> contain any binaries, please see below for those.</p>
<p>To verify your download please use the following SHA-1 checksums:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="3f5bc4b1cc2c28646891b1dbce286966fff64feb  wxMSW-3.1.5-Setup.exe

<h2>Binaries</h2>
<p>We provide pre-built binary files for the following compilers:</p>
<ul>
<li>Microsoft Visual C++ compiler versions 9.0, 10.0, 11.0, 12.0, 14.0, 14.1 and 14.2 (corresponding to marketing product names of Microsoft Visual Studio 2008, 2010, 2012, 2013, 2015, 2017 and 2019 respectively). Please note that MSVC 14.x versions are ABI-compatible and the same set of binaries is used for all of them.</li>
<li>MinGW-w64 versions 7.3 and 8.1 (32-bit binaries use SJLJ exceptions, 64-bit ones use SEH, and all binaries use Win32 threads).</li>
<li><a href="https://jmeubank.github.io/tdm-gcc/" rel="nofollow">TDM-GCC</a> 9.2.0.</li>
<li>Gcc-10.2.0 from the <a href="https://www.msys2.org/" rel="nofollow">MSYS2</a> project</li>
</ul>
<h3>For Developers</h3>
<p>For developing applications with wxWidgets you need to download the compiler-independent <code>wxWidgets-3.1.5_Headers.7z</code> file and one of <code>wxMSW-3.1.5-vcXXX_Dev.7z</code> or <code>wxMSW-3.1.5_gccXXX_Dev.7z</code> files depending on your compiler, its version and the target architecture (x86 if not specified or x64).</p>
<p>Unpack both files into the same directory so that <code>include</code> and <code>lib</code> directories are at the same level after unpacking. You should be able to compile and link applications using wxWidgets in both debug and release modes but the debug symbols are provided only for debug libraries in this archive, see below for the release build debug symbols.</p>
<p>Note that if you're setting up a new project using these binaries, the simplest<br>
way to do it is to use the provided <code>wxwidgets.props</code> file: for this, open the<br>
<code>View|Property Manager</code> menu item in the IDE, select "Add Existing Property<br>
Sheet..." from the project context menu and browse to this file in the file<br>
open dialog.</p>
<h3>For End Users</h3>
<p>End users may download one of <code>wxMSW-3.1.5_vcXXX_ReleaseDLL.7z</code> or <code>wxMSW-3.1.5_gccXXX_ReleaseDLL.7z</code> files to get just the DLLs required for running the applications using wxWidgets.</p>
<h3>For Debugging</h3>
<ul>
<li>Microsoft Visual C++ users: Files <code>wxMSW-3.1.5_vcXXX_ReleasePDB.7z</code> contain the debug symbols for the release build of the DLLs. Download them if you want to debug your own applications in release build or if you want to get meaningful information from mini-dumps retrieved from your users machines.</li>
<li>MinGW-TDM users: Currently the debug symbols are not available for the release build of the DLLs (only the debug versions of the DLLs contains the debug symbols).</li>
</ul>

<div class="d-flex flex-row mb-3">
  <div class="flex-1" data-pjax="#repo-content-pjax-container">
    <h1 data-view-component="true" class="d-inline mr-3"><a href="/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/tag/v3.1.4" data-view-component="true" class="Link--primary">wxWidgets 3.1.4</a></h1>

        <div data-pjax="true" data-test-selector="body-content" data-view-component="true" class="markdown-body my-3"><p>Welcome to wxWidgets, a free and open source cross-platform C++ framework for writing advanced GUI applications using native controls.</p>
<p>wxWidgets 3.1.4 is the latest release in the 3.1 development branch. This release is a "development" one as it makes (very few) incompatible API changes compared to 3.0 and does not guarantee the ABI stability, unlike the 3.0.x series. It is not inherently more buggy or less stable than the "stable" releases and you're encouraged to use it, including in production. If you're already using 3.0, upgrading shouldn't require any special effort, so please try it out.</p>
<p>Please see <a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/v3.1.4/docs/readme.txt" rel="nofollow"><strong>README</strong></a> for more information about this release and the <a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/v3.1.4/docs/changes.txt" rel="nofollow">change log</a> for more details of the changes in it.</p>
<h2>Source Files and Documentation</h2>
<p>If you intend to build wxWidgets from sources (which is recommended), please do <strong>NOT</strong> download the files using the "Source code" links just above, which are automatically generated by GitHub and don't contain the submodules sources which are necessary for building wxWidgets.</p>
<p>Instead, download one of <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.4/wxWidgets-3.1.4.zip">wxWidgets-3.1.4.zip</a> or <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.4/wxWidgets-3.1.4.7z">wxWidgets-3.1.4.7z</a>, for much smaller size, for Microsoft Windows systems or <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.4/wxWidgets-3.1.4.tar.bz2">wxWidgets-3.1.4.tar.bz2</a> for Unix ones, including macOS. These archives have exactly the same contents, but use the line endings appropriate for the corresponding platform.</p>
<p>In addition, we provide archives containing the documentation in either HTML or Microsoft CHM formats. Notice that the documentation is also <a href="https://docs.wxwidgets.org/3.1.4" rel="nofollow">available online</a>.</p>
<p>Finally, Microsoft Windows users may download <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.4/wxMSW-3.1.4-Setup.exe">Setup.exe file</a> containing both sources and documentation, however please note that this file does <em>not</em> contain any binaries, please see below for those.</p>
<p>To verify your download please use the following SHA-1 checksums:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="7e19253507156efc61dd8657af798177717775fe  wxMSW-3.1.4-Setup.exe

<h2>Binaries</h2>
<p>We provide pre-built binary files for the following compilers:</p>
<ul>
<li>Microsoft Visual C++ compiler versions 9.0, 10.0, 11.0, 12.0, 14.0, 14.1 and 14.2 (corresponding to marketing product names of Microsoft Visual Studio 2008, 2010, 2012, 2013, 2015, 2017 and 2019 respectively).</li>
<li>MinGW-w64 versions 7.3 and 8.1 (32-bit binaries use SJLJ exceptions, 64-bit ones use SEH, and all binaries use Win32 threads).</li>
<li><a href="https://jmeubank.github.io/tdm-gcc/" rel="nofollow">TDM-GCC</a> 9.2.0.</li>
</ul>
<h3>For Developers</h3>
<p>For developing applications with wxWidgets you need to download the compiler-independent <code>wxWidgets-3.1.4_Headers.7z</code> file and one of <code>wxMSW-3.1.4-vcXXX_Dev.7z</code> or <code>wxMSW-3.1.4_gccXXX_Dev.7z</code> files depending on your compiler, its version and the target architecture (x86 if not specified or x64).</p>
<p>Unpack both files into the same directory so that <code>include</code> and <code>lib</code> directories are at the same level after unpacking. You should be able to compile and link applications using wxWidgets in both debug and release modes but the debug symbols are provided only for debug libraries in this archive, see below for the release build debug symbols.</p>
<p>Note that if you're setting up a new project using these binaries, the simplest<br>
way to do it is to use the provided <code>wxwidgets.props</code> file: for this, open the<br>
<code>View|Property Manager</code> menu item in the IDE, select "Add Existing Property<br>
Sheet..." from the project context menu and browse to this file in the file<br>
open dialog.</p>
<h3>For End Users</h3>
<p>End users may download one of <code>wxMSW-3.1.4_vcXXX_ReleaseDLL.7z</code> or <code>wxMSW-3.1.4_gccXXX_ReleaseDLL.7z</code> files to get just the DLLs required for running the applications using wxWidgets.</p>
<h3>For Debugging</h3>
<ul>
<li>Microsoft Visual C++ users: Files <code>wxMSW-3.1.4_vcXXX_ReleasePDB.7z</code> contain the debug symbols for the release build of the DLLs. Download them if you want to debug your own applications in release build or if you want to get meaningful information from mini-dumps retrieved from your users machines.</li>
<li>MinGW-TDM users: Currently the debug symbols are not available for the release build of the DLLs (only the debug versions of the DLLs contains the debug symbols).</li>
</ul>

        <div data-pjax="true" data-test-selector="body-content" data-view-component="true" class="markdown-body my-3"><p>This is a patch release updating the soname of the shared libraries for Unix/ELF systems which was forgotten in 3.0.5. Because of this, please use the source archives from this release if you're building wxWidgets shared libraries from source under these systems, but please refer to 3.0.5 files for all the rest, i.e. MSW binaries and the documentation.</p>
<p>For completeness, the only other changes compared to 3.0.5 are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Workaround for the problem with overflowing maximum command line length in MinGW builds <em>not</em> using configure.</li>
<li>Fix for a problem with <code>wxSpinCtrl</code> in wxGTK, see <a href="https://trac.wxwidgets.org/ticket/18688" rel="nofollow">#18688</a>.</li>
</ul>

    <h1 data-view-component="true" class="d-inline mr-3"><a href="/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/tag/v3.0.5" data-view-component="true" class="Link--primary">wxWidgets 3.0.5</a></h1>

        <div data-pjax="true" data-test-selector="body-content" data-view-component="true" class="markdown-body my-3"><p>Welcome to wxWidgets, a free and open source cross-platform C++ framework for writing advanced GUI applications using native controls.</p>
<p>Please notice that since the 2.9 series, only a single source distribution is provided instead of the multiple distributions containing only the files for each port as was done before. So you only need to download wxWidgets-3.0.5.zip (or .7z for much smaller archive size) for Microsoft Windows systems or wxWidgets-3.0.5.tar.bz2 for Unix ones, including Mac OS X. The only difference between these files is that the ZIP (and 7z) archives contain files with DOS line endings while the tar balls contain files with Unix line endings.</p>
<p>See <a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/v3.0.5/docs/readme.txt" rel="nofollow">README</a> for more information about this release and the <a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/v3.0.5/docs/changes.txt" rel="nofollow">change log</a> for details of the changes in it.</p>
<h2>Reporting Problems</h2>
<p>Please report bugs to the <a href="http://trac.wxwidgets.org/newticket" rel="nofollow">issue tracker</a> or the <a href="http://groups.google.com/group/wx-users" rel="nofollow">wx-users mailing list</a>.</p>
<h2>Download Verification</h2>
<p>To verify your download please use the following sha1sums:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="763ee2656409e6fe699a482ccf37bb2aebb3cee9  wxMSW-3.0.5-Setup.exe

<h2>Binaries</h2>
<p>We have provided pre-built binary files for the following compilers:</p>
<ul>
<li>Microsoft Visual C++ compiler versions 9.0, 10.0, 11.0, 12.0, 14.0, 14.1 and 14.2, corresponding to marketing product names of Microsoft Visual Studio 2008, 2010, 2012, 2013, 2015, 2017 and 2019 respectively.</li>
<li>TDM-GCC version 4.9.2, 5.1.0, 9.2.0 and MinGW-w64 version 7.2.0, 7.3.0 and 8.1.0 (with the default SJLJ exceptions propagation method for 32 bits architectures and SEH one for 64 bits, using C++11). Please note that for MinGW-w64 7.2.0,  you need to use the very latest release which can be downloaded from <a href="https://sourceforge.net/projects/mingw-w64/files/Toolchains%20targetting%20Win32/Personal%20Builds/mingw-builds/7.2.0/threads-win32/sjlj/i686-7.2.0-release-win32-sjlj-rt_v5-rev1.7z/download" rel="nofollow">here for 32 bits</a> and <a href="https://sourceforge.net/projects/mingw-w64/files/Toolchains%20targetting%20Win64/Personal%20Builds/mingw-builds/7.2.0/threads-win32/seh/x86_64-7.2.0-release-win32-seh-rt_v5-rev1.7z/download" rel="nofollow">here for 64 bits</a>, the older "rev0" release has a known bug affecting building wxWidgets in some scenarios.</li>
</ul>
<h3>For Developers</h3>
<p>For developing applications with wxWidgets you need to download the compiler-independent <code>wxWidgets-3.0.5_Headers.7z</code> file and one of <code>wxMSW-3.0.5-vcXXX_Dev.7z</code> or <code>wxMSW-3.0.5_gccXXX_Dev.7z</code> files depending on your compiler, its version and the target architecture (x86 if not specified or x64).</p>
<p>Unpack both files into the same directory so that <code>include</code> and <code>lib</code> directories are at the same level after unpacking. You should be able to compile and link applications using wxWidgets in both debug and release modes but the debug symbols are provided only for debug libraries in this archive, see below for the release build debug symbols.</p>
<h3>For End Users</h3>
<p>End users may download one of <code>wxMSW-3.0.5_vcXXX_ReleaseDLL.7z</code> or <code>wxMSW-3.0.5_gccXXX_ReleaseDLL.7z</code> files to get just the DLLs required for running the applications using wxWidgets.</p>
<h3>For Debugging</h3>
<ul>
<li>Microsoft Visual C++ users: Files <code>wxMSW-3.0.5_vcXXX_ReleasePDB.7z</code> contain the debug symbols for the release build of the DLLs. Download them if you want to debug your own applications in release build or if you want to get meaningful information from mini-dumps retrieved from your users machines.</li>
<li>MinGW-TDM and MinGW-w64 users: Currently the debug symbols are not available for the release build of the DLLs (only the debug versions of the DLLs contains the debug symbols).</li>
</ul>

  <div class="flex-1" data-pjax="#repo-content-pjax-container">
    <h1 data-view-component="true" class="d-inline mr-3"><a href="/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/tag/v3.1.3" data-view-component="true" class="Link--primary">wxWidgets 3.1.3</a></h1>

        <div data-pjax="true" data-test-selector="body-content" data-view-component="true" class="markdown-body my-3"><p>Welcome to wxWidgets, a free and open source cross-platform C++ framework for writing advanced GUI applications using native controls.</p>
<p>wxWidgets 3.1.3 is the latest release in the 3.1 development branch. This release is a "development" one as it makes (very few) incompatible API changes compared to 3.0 and does not guarantee the ABI stability, unlike the 3.0.x series. It is not inherently more buggy or less stable than the "stable" releases and you're encouraged to use it, including in production. If you're already using 3.0, upgrading shouldn't require any special effort, so please try it out.</p>
<p>Please see <a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/v3.1.3/docs/readme.txt" rel="nofollow"><strong>README</strong></a> for more information about this release and the <a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/v3.1.3/docs/changes.txt" rel="nofollow">change log</a> for the details of the changes in it.</p>
<h2>Source Files and Documentation</h2>
<p>If you intend to build wxWidgets from sources (which is recommended), please do <strong>NOT</strong> download the files using the "Source code" links just above, which are automatically generated by GitHub and don't contain the submodules sources which are necessary for building wxWidgets.</p>
<p>Instead, download one of <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.3/wxWidgets-3.1.3.zip">wxWidgets-3.1.3.zip</a> or <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.3/wxWidgets-3.1.3.7z">wxWidgets-3.1.3.7z</a>, for much smaller size, for Microsoft Windows systems or <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.3/wxWidgets-3.1.3.tar.bz2">wxWidgets-3.1.3.tar.bz2</a> for Unix ones, including macOS. These archives have exactly the same contents, but use the line endings appropriate for the corresponding platform.</p>
<p>In addition, we provide archives containing the documentation in either HTML or Microsoft CHM formats. Notice that the documentation is also <a href="https://docs.wxwidgets.org/3.1.3" rel="nofollow">available online</a>.</p>
<p>Finally, Microsoft Windows users may download <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.3/wxMSW-3.1.3-Setup.exe">Setup.exe file</a> containing both sources and documentation, however please note that this file does <em>not</em> contain any binaries, please see below for those.</p>
<p>To verify your download please use the following SHA-1 checksums:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="393a91afb64ee989bf986677a4aa5597acf6ed6d  wxMSW-3.1.3-Setup.exe

<h2>Binaries</h2>
<p>We provide pre-built binary files for the following compilers:</p>
<ul>
<li>Microsoft Visual C++ compiler versions 9.0, 10.0, 11.0, 12.0, 14.0, 14.1 and 14.2 (corresponding to marketing product names of Microsoft Visual Studio 2008, 2010, 2012, 2013, 2015, 2017 and 2019 respectively).</li>
<li>MinGW-w64 versions 7.3 and 8.1 (with the default SJLJ exceptions propagation method, using C++11).</li>
</ul>
<h3>For Developers</h3>
<p>For developing applications with wxWidgets you need to download the compiler-independent <code>wxWidgets-3.1.3_Headers.7z</code> file and one of <code>wxMSW-3.1.3-vcXXX_Dev.7z</code> or <code>wxMSW-3.1.3_gccXXX_Dev.7z</code> files depending on your compiler, its version and the target architecture (x86 if not specified or x64).</p>
<p>Unpack both files into the same directory so that <code>include</code> and <code>lib</code> directories are at the same level after unpacking. You should be able to compile and link applications using wxWidgets in both debug and release modes but the debug symbols are provided only for debug libraries in this archive, see below for the release build debug symbols.</p>
<p>Note that if you're setting up a new project using these binaries, the simplest way to do it is to use the provided <code>wxwidgets.props</code> file: for this, open the <code>View|Property Manager</code> menu item in the IDE, select "Add Existing Property Sheet..." from the project context menu and browse to this file in the file open dialog.</p>
<h3>For End Users</h3>
<p>End users may download one of <code>wxMSW-3.1.3_vcXXX_ReleaseDLL.7z</code> or <code>wxMSW-3.1.3_gccXXX_ReleaseDLL.7z</code> files to get just the DLLs required for running the applications using wxWidgets.</p>
<h3>For Debugging</h3>
<ul>
<li>Microsoft Visual C++ users: Files <code>wxMSW-3.1.3_vcXXX_ReleasePDB.7z</code> contain the debug symbols for the release build of the DLLs. Download them if you want to debug your own applications in release build or if you want to get meaningful information from mini-dumps retrieved from your users machines.</li>
<li>MinGW-w64 users: Currently the debug symbols are not available for the release build of the DLLs (only the debug versions of the DLLs contains the debug symbols).</li>
</ul>

<p>To verify your download please use the following SHA-1 checksums:</p>

        <div data-pjax="true" data-test-selector="body-content" data-view-component="true" class="markdown-body my-3"><p>Welcome to wxWidgets, a free and open source cross-platform C++ framework for writing advanced GUI applications using native controls.</p>
<p>wxWidgets 3.1.2 is the latest release in the 3.1 development branch. This release is a "development" one as it makes (very few) incompatible API changes compared to 3.0 and does not guarantee the ABI stability, unlike the 3.0.x series. It is not inherently more buggy or less stable than the "stable" releases and you're encouraged to use it, including in production. If you're already using 3.0, upgrading shouldn't require any special effort, so please try it out.</p>
<p>Please see <a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/v3.1.2/docs/readme.txt" rel="nofollow"><strong>README</strong></a> for more information about this release and the <a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/v3.1.2/docs/changes.txt" rel="nofollow">change log</a> for the details of the changes in it.</p>
<h2>Source Files and Documentation</h2>
<p>If you intend to build wxWidgets from sources (which is recommended), please do <strong>NOT</strong> download the files using the "Source code" links just above, which are automatically generated by GitHub and don't contain the submodules sources which are necessary for building wxWidgets.</p>
<p>Instead, download one of <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.2/wxWidgets-3.1.2.zip">wxWidgets-3.1.2.zip</a> or <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.2/wxWidgets-3.1.2.7z">wxWidgets-3.1.2.7z</a>, for much smaller size, for Microsoft Windows systems or <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.2/wxWidgets-3.1.2.tar.bz2">wxWidgets-3.1.2.tar.bz2</a> for Unix ones, including macOS. These archives have exactly the same contents, but use the line endings appropriate for the corresponding platform.</p>
<p>In addition, we provide archives containing the documentation in either HTML or Microsoft CHM formats. Notice that the documentation is also <a href="https://docs.wxwidgets.org/3.1.2" rel="nofollow">available online</a>.</p>
<p>Finally, Microsoft Windows users may download <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.2/wxMSW-3.1.2-Setup.exe">Setup.exe file</a> containing both sources and documentation, however please note that this file does <em>not</em> contain any binaries, please see below for those.</p>
<p>To verify your download please use the following SHA-1 checksums:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="85ac5b18de191d9d5504b7106466b21b64e7249d  wxMSW-3.1.2-Setup.exe

<h2>Binaries</h2>
<p>We provide pre-built binary files for the following compilers:</p>
<ul>
<li>Microsoft Visual C++ compiler versions 9.0, 10.0, 11.0, 12.0, 14.0 and 14.1 (corresponding to marketing product names of Microsoft Visual Studio 2008, 2010, 2012, 2013, 2015 and 2017 respectively).</li>
<li>TDM-GCC version 5.1 and MinGW-w64 versions 7.3 and 8.1 (with the default SJLJ exceptions propagation method, using C++11).</li>
</ul>
<h3>For Developers</h3>
<p>For developing applications with wxWidgets you need to download the compiler-independent <code>wxWidgets-3.1.2_Headers.7z</code> file and one of <code>wxMSW-3.1.2-vcXXX_Dev.7z</code> or <code>wxMSW-3.1.2_gccXXX_Dev.7z</code> files depending on your compiler, its version and the target architecture (x86 if not specified or x64).</p>
<p>Unpack both files into the same directory so that <code>include</code> and <code>lib</code> directories are at the same level after unpacking. You should be able to compile and link applications using wxWidgets in both debug and release modes but the debug symbols are provided only for debug libraries in this archive, see below for the release build debug symbols.</p>
<h3>For End Users</h3>
<p>End users may download one of <code>wxMSW-3.1.2_vcXXX_ReleaseDLL.7z</code> or <code>wxMSW-3.1.2_gccXXX_ReleaseDLL.7z</code> files to get just the DLLs required for running the applications using wxWidgets.</p>
<h3>For Debugging</h3>
<ul>
<li>Microsoft Visual C++ users: Files <code>wxMSW-3.1.2_vcXXX_ReleasePDB.7z</code> contain the debug symbols for the release build of the DLLs. Download them if you want to debug your own applications in release build or if you want to get meaningful information from mini-dumps retrieved from your users machines.</li>
<li>MinGW-TDM users: Currently the debug symbols are not available for the release build of the DLLs (only the debug versions of the DLLs contains the debug symbols).</li>
</ul>

    <h1 data-view-component="true" class="d-inline mr-3"><a href="/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/tag/v3.0.4" data-view-component="true" class="Link--primary">wxWidgets 3.0.4</a></h1>

        <div data-pjax="true" data-test-selector="body-content" data-view-component="true" class="markdown-body my-3"><p>Welcome to wxWidgets, a free and open source cross-platform C++ framework for writing advanced GUI applications using native controls.</p>
<p>Please notice that since the 2.9 series, only a single source distribution is provided instead of the multiple distributions containing only the files for each port as was done before. So you only need to download wxWidgets-3.0.0.zip (or .7z for much smaller archive size) for Microsoft Windows systems or wxWidgets-3.0.0.tar.bz2 for Unix ones, including Mac OS X. The only difference between these files is that the ZIP (and 7z) archives contain files with DOS line endings while the tar balls contain files with Unix line endings.</p>
<p>See <a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/v3.0.4/docs/readme.txt" rel="nofollow">README</a> for more information about this release and the <a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/v3.0.4/docs/changes.txt" rel="nofollow">change log</a> for details of the changes in it.</p>
<h2>Reporting Problems</h2>
<p>Please report bugs to the <a href="http://trac.wxwidgets.org/newticket" rel="nofollow">issue tracker</a> or the <a href="http://groups.google.com/group/wx-users" rel="nofollow">wx-users mailing list</a>.</p>
<h2>Download Verification</h2>
<p>To verify your download please use the following sha1sums:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="fd905711464591c75cfc6c9704eb37f77005543f  wxMSW-3.0.4-Setup.exe

<h2>Binaries</h2>
<p>We have provided pre-built binary files for the following compilers:</p>
<ul>
<li>Microsoft Visual C++ compiler versions 9.0, 10.0, 11.0, 12.0, 14.0 and 14.1, corresponding to marketing product names of Microsoft Visual Studio 2008, 2010, 2012, 2013, 2015 and 2017 respectively.</li>
<li>MinGW-TDM versions 4.9.2, 5.1.0 and MinGW 7.2.0 (with the default SJLJ exceptions propagation method, using C++11). Please note that you need to use the very latest MinGW 7.2 compiler release with this version of the compiler which can be downloaded from <a href="https://sourceforge.net/projects/mingw-w64/files/Toolchains%20targetting%20Win32/Personal%20Builds/mingw-builds/7.2.0/threads-win32/sjlj/i686-7.2.0-release-win32-sjlj-rt_v5-rev1.7z/download" rel="nofollow">here for 32 bits</a> and <a href="https://sourceforge.net/projects/mingw-w64/files/Toolchains%20targetting%20Win64/Personal%20Builds/mingw-builds/7.2.0/threads-win32/seh/x86_64-7.2.0-release-win32-seh-rt_v5-rev1.7z/download" rel="nofollow">here for 64 bits</a>, the older "rev0" release has a known bug affecting building wxWidgets in some scenarios.</li>
</ul>
<h3>For Developers</h3>
<p>For developing applications with wxWidgets you need to download the compiler-independent <code>wxWidgets-3.0.4_Headers.7z</code> file and one of <code>wxMSW-3.0.4-vcXXX_Dev.7z</code> or <code>wxMSW-3.0.4_gccXXX_Dev.7z</code> files depending on your compiler, its version and the target architecture (x86 if not specified or x64).</p>
<p>Unpack both files into the same directory so that <code>include</code> and <code>lib</code> directories are at the same level after unpacking. You should be able to compile and link applications using wxWidgets in both debug and release modes but the debug symbols are provided only for debug libraries in this archive, see below for the release build debug symbols.</p>
<h3>For End Users</h3>
<p>End users may download one of <code>wxMSW-3.0.4_vcXXX_ReleaseDLL.7z</code> or <code>wxMSW-3.0.4_gccXXX_ReleaseDLL.7z</code> files to get just the DLLs required for running the applications using wxWidgets.</p>
<h3>For Debugging</h3>
<ul>
<li>Microsoft Visual C++ users: Files <code>wxMSW-3.0.4_vcXXX_ReleasePDB.7z</code> contain the debug symbols for the release build of the DLLs. Download them if you want to debug your own applications in release build or if you want to get meaningful information from mini-dumps retrieved from your users machines.</li>
<li>MinGW and MinGW-TDM users: Currently the debug symbols are not available for the release build of the DLLs (only the debug versions of the DLLs contains the debug symbols).</li>
</ul>

    <h1 data-view-component="true" class="d-inline mr-3"><a href="/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/tag/v3.1.1" data-view-component="true" class="Link--primary">wxWidgets 3.1.1</a></h1>

        <div data-pjax="true" data-test-selector="body-content" data-view-component="true" class="markdown-body my-3"><p>Welcome to wxWidgets, a free and open source cross-platform C++ framework for writing advanced GUI applications using native controls.</p>
<p>wxWidgets 3.1.1 is the second release in the 3.1 development branch. This release is a "development" one as it makes (very few) incompatible API changes compared to 3.0 and does not guarantee the ABI stability, unlike the 3.0.x series. It is not inherently more buggy or less stable than the "stable" releases and you're encouraged to use it. If you're already using 3.0, upgrading shouldn't require any special effort, so please try it out.</p>
<p>Please see <a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/v3.1.1/docs/readme.txt" rel="nofollow"><strong>README</strong></a> for more information about this release and the <a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/v3.1.1/docs/changes.txt" rel="nofollow">change log</a> for details of the changes in it.</p>
<h2>Source Files and Documentation</h2>
<p>If you intend to build wxWidgets from sources (which is recommended), please do <strong>NOT</strong> download the files using the "Source code" links just above, which are automatically generated by GitHub and don't contain the submodules sources which are necessary for building wxWidgets.</p>
<p>Instead, download one of <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.1/wxWidgets-3.1.1.zip">wxWidgets-3.1.1.zip</a> or <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.1/wxWidgets-3.1.1.7z">wxWidgets-3.1.1.7z</a>, for much smaller size, for Microsoft Windows systems or <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.1/wxWidgets-3.1.1.tar.bz2">wxWidgets-3.1.1.tar.bz2</a> for Unix ones, including macOS. These archives have exactly the same contents, but use the line endings appropriate for the corresponding platform.</p>
<p>In addition, we provide archives containing the documentation in either HTML or Microsoft CHM formats. Notice that the documentation is also <a href="http://docs.wxwidgets.org/3.1" rel="nofollow">available online</a>.</p>
<p>Finally, Microsoft Windows users may download <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.1/wxMSW-3.1.1-Setup.exe">Setup.exe file</a> containing both sources and documentation, however please note that this file does <em>not</em> contain any binaries, please see below for those.</p>
<p>To verify your download please use the following SHA-1 checksums:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="155626101d1e532d5d58b3d85b31be99cee0dd58  wxMSW-3.1.1-Setup.exe

<h2>Binaries</h2>
<p>We provide pre-built binary files for the following compilers:</p>
<ul>
<li>Microsoft Visual C++ compiler versions 9.0, 10.0, 11.0, 12.0, 14.0 and 14.1 (corresponding to marketing product names of Microsoft Visual Studio 2008, 2010, 2012, 2013, 2015 and 2017 respectively).</li>
<li>MinGW-TDM versions 5.1 and 7.2 (with the default SJLJ exceptions propagation method, using C++11). Please note that you need to use the very latest MinGW 7.2 compiler release with this version of the compiler which can be downloaded from <a href="https://sourceforge.net/projects/mingw-w64/files/Toolchains%20targetting%20Win32/Personal%20Builds/mingw-builds/7.2.0/threads-win32/sjlj/i686-7.2.0-release-win32-sjlj-rt_v5-rev1.7z/download" rel="nofollow">here for 32 bits</a> and <a href="https://sourceforge.net/projects/mingw-w64/files/Toolchains%20targetting%20Win64/Personal%20Builds/mingw-builds/7.2.0/threads-win32/seh/x86_64-7.2.0-release-win32-seh-rt_v5-rev1.7z/download" rel="nofollow">here for 64 bits</a>, the older "rev0" release has a known bug affecting building wxWidgets in some scenarios.</li>
</ul>
<h3>For Developers</h3>
<p>For developing applications with wxWidgets you need to download the compiler-independent <code>wxWidgets-3.1.1_Headers.7z</code> file and one of <code>wxMSW-3.1.1-vcXXX_Dev.7z</code> or <code>wxMSW-3.1.1_gccXXX_Dev.7z</code> files depending on your compiler, its version and the target architecture (x86 if not specified or x64).</p>
<p>Unpack both files into the same directory so that <code>include</code> and <code>lib</code> directories are at the same level after unpacking. You should be able to compile and link applications using wxWidgets in both debug and release modes but the debug symbols are provided only for debug libraries in this archive, see below for the release build debug symbols.</p>
<h3>For End Users</h3>
<p>End users may download one of <code>wxMSW-3.1.1_vcXXX_ReleaseDLL.7z</code> or <code>wxMSW-3.1.1_gccXXX_ReleaseDLL.7z</code> files to get just the DLLs required for running the applications using wxWidgets.</p>
<h3>For Debugging</h3>
<ul>
<li>Microsoft Visual C++ users: Files <code>wxMSW-3.1.1_vcXXX_ReleasePDB.7z</code> contain the debug symbols for the release build of the DLLs. Download them if you want to debug your own applications in release build or if you want to get meaningful information from mini-dumps retrieved from your users machines.</li>
<li>MinGW-TDM users: Currently the debug symbols are not available for the release build of the DLLs (only the debug versions of the DLLs contains the debug<br>
symbols).</li>
</ul>

    <h1 data-view-component="true" class="d-inline mr-3"><a href="/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/tag/v3.1.1-rc" data-view-component="true" class="Link--primary">Release candidate for wxWidgets 3.1.1</a></h1>

        <div data-pjax="true" data-test-selector="body-content" data-view-component="true" class="markdown-body my-3"><p><em>WARNING</em> This is a release candidate and not the final 3.1.1 release yet.</p>
<p>Welcome to wxWidgets, a free and open source cross-platform C++ framework for writing advanced GUI applications using native controls.</p>
<p>wxWidgets 3.1.1 is the second release in the 3.1 development branch. This release is a "development" one as it makes (very few) incompatible API changes compared to 3.0 and does not guarantee the ABI stability, unlike the 3.0.x series. It is not inherently more buggy or less stable than the "stable" releases and you're encouraged to use it. If you're already using 3.0, upgrading shouldn't require any special effort, so please try it out.</p>
<p>Please see <a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/v3.1.1-rc/docs/readme.txt" rel="nofollow"><strong>README</strong></a> for more information about this release and the <a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/v3.1.1-rc/docs/changes.txt" rel="nofollow">change log</a> for details of the changes in it.</p>
<h2>Source Files and Documentation</h2>
<p>If you intend to build wxWidgets from sources (which is recommended), please do <strong>NOT</strong> download the files using the "Source code" links just above, which are automatically generated by GitHub and don't contain the submodules sources which are necessary for building wxWidgets.</p>
<p>Instead, download one of <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.1-rc/wxWidgets-3.1.1-rc.zip">wxWidgets-3.1.1-rc.zip</a> or <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.1-rc/wxWidgets-3.1.1-rc.7z">wxWidgets-3.1.1-rc.7z</a>, for much smaller size, for Microsoft Windows systems or <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.1-rc/wxWidgets-3.1.1-rc.tar.bz2">wxWidgets-3.1.1-rc.tar.bz2</a> for Unix ones, including macOS. These archives have exactly the same contents, but use the line endings appropriate for the corresponding platform.</p>
<p>In addition, we provide archives containing the documentation in either HTML or Microsoft CHM formats. Notice that the documentation is also <a href="http://docs.wxwidgets.org/3.1" rel="nofollow">available online</a>.</p>
<p>Finally, Microsoft Windows users may download <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/download/v3.1.1-rc/wxMSW-3.1.1-rc-Setup.exe">Setup.exe file</a> containing both sources and documentation, however please note that this file does <em>not</em> contain any binaries, please see below for those.</p>
<p>To verify your download please use the following SHA-1 checksums:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="d3f8a8f5bd7b5dee2176a14fce93b3767d217f00  wxMSW-3.1.1-rc-Setup.exe

<h2>Binaries</h2>
<p>We provide pre-built binary files for the following compilers:</p>
<ul>
<li>Microsoft Visual C++ compiler versions 9.0, 10.0, 11.0, 12.0, 14.0 and 14.1 (corresponding to marketing product names of Microsoft Visual Studio 2008, 2010, 2012, 2013, 2015 and 2017 respectively).</li>
<li>MinGW-TDM versions 5.1 and 7.2 (with the default SJLJ exceptions propagation method, using C++11). Please note that you need to use the very latest MinGW 7.2 compiler release with this version of the compiler which can be downloaded from <a href="https://sourceforge.net/projects/mingw-w64/files/Toolchains%20targetting%20Win32/Personal%20Builds/mingw-builds/7.2.0/threads-win32/sjlj/i686-7.2.0-release-win32-sjlj-rt_v5-rev1.7z/download" rel="nofollow">here for 32 bits</a> and <a href="https://sourceforge.net/projects/mingw-w64/files/Toolchains%20targetting%20Win64/Personal%20Builds/mingw-builds/7.2.0/threads-win32/seh/x86_64-7.2.0-release-win32-seh-rt_v5-rev1.7z/download" rel="nofollow">here for 64 bits</a>, the older "rev0" release has a known bug affecting building wxWidgets in some scenarios.</li>
</ul>
<h3>For Developers</h3>
<p>For developing applications with wxWidgets you need to download the compiler-independent <code>wxWidgets-3.1.1_Headers.7z</code> file and one of <code>wxMSW-3.1.1-vcXXX_Dev.7z</code> or <code>wxMSW-3.1.1_gccXXX_Dev.7z</code> files depending on your compiler, its version and the target architecture (x86 if not specified or x64).</p>
<p>Unpack both files into the same directory so that <code>include</code> and <code>lib</code> directories are at the same level after unpacking. You should be able to compile and link applications using wxWidgets in both debug and release modes but the debug symbols are provided only for debug libraries in this archive, see below for the release build debug symbols.</p>
<h3>For End Users</h3>
<p>End users may download one of <code>wxMSW-3.1.1_vcXXX_ReleaseDLL.7z</code> or <code>wxMSW-3.1.1_gccXXX_ReleaseDLL.7z</code> files to get just the DLLs required for running the applications using wxWidgets.</p>
<h3>For Debugging</h3>
<ul>
<li>Microsoft Visual C++ users: Files <code>wxMSW-3.1.1_vcXXX_ReleasePDB.7z</code> contain the debug symbols for the release build of the DLLs. Download them if you want to debug your own applications in release build or if you want to get meaningful information from mini-dumps retrieved from your users machines.</li>
<li>MinGW-TDM users: Currently the debug symbols are not available for the release build of the DLLs (only the debug versions of the DLLs contains the debug<br>
symbols).</li>
</ul>

<h2>Reporting Problems</h2>
<p>Please report bugs to the <a href="https://trac.wxwidgets.org/newticket" rel="nofollow">issue tracker</a> or the <a href="http://groups.google.com/group/wx-users" rel="nofollow">wx-users mailing list</a>.</p></div>

    <div class="col-md-9" data-test-selector="release-card" >
  <div data-view-component="true" class="Box">
  
  <div data-view-component="true" class="Box-body">        <div class="float-right d-none d-md-block">
                  <div class="d-flex flex-items-center ml-md-5 mt-md-3">
            </div>

  </div>

<div class="d-flex flex-row mb-3">
  <div class="flex-1" data-pjax="#repo-content-pjax-container">
    <h1 data-view-component="true" class="d-inline mr-3"><a href="/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/tag/v3.0.3.1" data-view-component="true" class="Link--primary">Bug fix release for 3.0.3</a></h1>
    
      <div class="v-align-text-bottom ml-2 d-none d-md-inline">
          
      </div>
  </div>

  <div class="mt-3 d-md-none">
    
  </div>
      <div class="ml-2 mt-3 d-md-none">
        
      </div>
</div>


  <div class="d-md-none border-bottom mb-4 pb-4">
                  <div class="d-flex flex-items-center ml-md-5 mt-md-3">
            </div>

  </div>
        <div data-pjax="true" data-test-selector="body-content" data-view-component="true" class="markdown-body my-3"><p>This is almost exactly the same as the <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/tag/v3.0.3">last release</a> but includes the missing <code>wxPropertySheetDialog::SetInnerSize()</code> method which was mistakenly removed from 3.0.3.</p>
<p>Please notice that this method is undocumented and not supposed to be used from outside the library and it is declared as inline and thus is not part of the library ABI, so its absence in 3.0.3 normally shouldn't affect the library users, so there is no need to update unless, for some reason, you need to recompile existing code using this method with the latest sources, as is the case when building <a href="http://www.wxperl.it/" rel="nofollow">wxPerl</a>, for example.</p>
<p>Otherwise please continue using <a href="https://github.com/wxWidgets/wxWidgets/releases/tag/v3.0.3">3.0.3 release</a> and, in particular, the binaries and documentations provided for it as they are unchanged for this release.</p>

<p>To verify your download please use the following sha1sums:</p>
